CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication, dated July 9, 200 I from
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President, Cook County Board of Commissioners
I hereby trans mit a request that the Cook County Board of Commissioners enter into a contract with
Susan J. White & Associates, Inc. (SJWA), Alexandria, Virginia, to provide federal government relations
consulting services to Cook County. Compensation for these services sha ll be at a rate of $10,000.00 per
month and include reimbursement expenses not to exceed $ 10,000.00.
Reason:

T he scope of services shall include but are not limited to leading and coordinating services in
re lation to federal initiatives regarding health care, welfare and immigration reform, fede ral
crime legislation and regulatory concerns. Ms. White's knowledge of both federal and local
government has been an asset to Cook County for the past three years.

Esti mated Fiscal Impact: $ 130,000.00. Contract period: July I, 2001 through June 30, 2002. (490-260
Account).
Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri , moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commi ssioner Hansen, moved that the request of the County
Purchasing Agent be authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried.

Commissioner Moran voted "no".

COMM UN ITY DEV ELOPMENT BLOCK GRANT PROGRAM
T ransmitting a Communication, dated June 1 I, 200 I from
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President, Cook County Board of Commissioners
Transmitted herewith are the recommended projects for the 200 I Community Development Block Grant
program (CDBG), the Emergency Shelter Grants Program (ESG), and the HOME Investment Partnership
Prog ram ( HOM E) (October I , 200 I throug h September 30, 2002). The Cook County Community
Development Adv isory Council adopted these recommendations at a public hearing held on May 3 1,
2001 .

The amount of CDBG funds requested was $27,906,946.00. The amount of CDBG funds avai lable for
programming is $ 13,562,000.00. The proposed use of C DBG funds w ill provide a I 00% benefit to low
and moderate income persons.

The amount of ESG funds requested was $ 1,261 , 11 7.00. The amount of ESG fund s avai lable for
programming is $43 1,000.00. The proposed use of ESG funds provides essential services and
mai ntenance/operational costs fo r homeless shelters in suburban Cook County, as well as programs for
homeless prevention.

The amount of HOM E In vestment Partnership funds g ranted by the U.S. Departm ent of Housing and
Urban Development (HUD) is $6,279,000.00. Applications fo r eligible HOME projects are accepted
throughout the year. The proposed use of all funds must be incorporated into the County 's Annual Action
Plan for submittal to HUD.

Prior to subm itting required documents to HUD, Cook County is req uired by Execut ive Order 12372,
Intergovernmental Review of Federal Programs, to s ubmit proposed projects to the North eastern Illinois
Planning Commission and the Illinois State Clearing house for their review and release to HUD. The
County must also publish the description of the Annual Action Plan. All documents and certificati ons
must be submitted to HUD no later than A ug ust 15, 200 I.

1 respectfull y req uest approval of the recommended CDBG and ESG projects, the proposed use of the
HO ME fund s, and that I or the C hi ef Admini strative Officer of the County of Cook, or hi s designee, be
authori zed to execute on behalf of the County of Cook any and all documents necessary to further the
programs approved herein, including but not limited to subgrantee ag reements, intergovernm ental
agreements, amendments and modifi cation thereto, loan documents, lien assignments, re leases of
mortgages and liens, and mo rtgage assumptions.

Commissio ner Silvestri , seconded by Commissioner Carr, moved that the request of the President of the
Cook County Board Commi ssio ners be approved. T he motion carried unanimously.

COMMISSIONERS
PROPOSED RESOLUTIONS
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
WILLIAM R. MORAN, County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

WHEREAS, the Highway Department of Cook County has the duty and responsibil ity to monitor and
determine the need for improvements to the Highway System of Cook County for the County of Cook,
said improvements being required to address safety and/or capacity deficiencies experienced by the
motoring public; and
WHEREAS, it is in the best interest of the motoring public that these highway improvements be
completed as expeditiously as possible; and
WHEREAS, the res idents of Cook County li ving a long Holbrook Road between Halsted Street and Dixie
Highway have complained about the speed and traffic from trucks exceeding the weight limits for
Holbrook Road; and
WHEREAS, Holbrook Road between Ha lsted Street and Dixie Highway is a County Highway, under the
control of the Cook County Board of Commissioners and the Cook County Highway Department; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners is granted the power to place s igns o n County
Highways by the Illinois Vehicle Code; and
WHEREAS, Sheriff Officers have stated they can not issue tickets for exceeding the weight limit for
Holbrook Road unless adequate signs are placed along Holbrook Road indicating the weight limit and/or
an alternate truck route; and
WHEREAS, the current truck traffic creates terrible conditions for the residents along and motorists on
Holbrook Road.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and Members of the Cook County Board
of Commissioners authorize the Cook County Highway Department to take all action necessary in order
to place adequate signs along Holbrook Road indicating either the weight limits for vehicles or an
alternate route for vehicles in excess of the weight limit for Holbrook Road from Halsted Street to Dixie
Highway.
Comm issioner Moran, seconded by Comm issioner Carr, moved that the Proposed Resol ution be referred
to the Comm ittee on Roads and Bridges. (Comm. No. 244840). The motion carried unanimously.

* * * * *
Subm itting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
WILLIAM R. MORAN, County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

WHEREAS, Cook County makes a substantial investment in terms of time and money in providing for
the training of newly hired employees for the Sheriffs Office; and

2295

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR J ULY I 0, 200 I

WHEREAS, the Sheriff is entitled to expect a reasonab le return on such investment, in terms of the
commitment and devotion to duty of their prospective employees; and
WHEREAS, it has become prevalent for employees to leave the Sheriffs Office and the community,
which provided their training and equipment before a reasonable amount of time has passed;

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED BY
COMMISSIONERS AS FOLLOWS:

THE COOK

COUNTY

BOARD

OF

Section 1 - Title
This Resolution shall be known as the Cook County Training Re imbursement Agreement.

Section 2 - Scope
This Reso lutio n applies to a ll no n-civilian employees of the Sheriff s Office w ho receive equ ipment
and/or training for their position with the Sheriff' s Office, including but not limited to Deputy Sheriff's,
Correction' s Officers, Court Services Officers and Commun ity Services Officers.

Section 3 - Agreement
I.

T he Cook County Sheriff's Employee withi n the scope of this Resolution (" Employee") agrees to
pa1ticipate in the Sheriffs required law enforcement training. The Employee further agrees to
s uccessfully complete s uch training and obtain the necessary and appropriate certification. The
Employee then agrees to serve as an Employee of the Cook County Sheri ff's Office. Said
Employee does further agree to devote full-time to the training and subseq uent service and to
perform a ll assig nments in a satisfactory manner.

2.

T he Sheriff agrees to make available to the Employee law enforcement train ing as set fo rth
above. and to be responsible for and to pay for a ll re lated expenses in connection therewith,
including equipment and salaries on the premises while the Empl oyee is in training, if required,
and further, to provide in-house training for the Em ployee during the periods of time that said
Employee is employed with the Sheriff' s Office, but not attendi ng the training academy.

3.

The cost and expenses related to the training and equipping of the Employee change with time
along with any increase in expenses, changing the cost of a breach of this Agreement by the
Employee. Any Employee found to have violated this agreement agrees to pay the County the
s um of:
The cost of training the Employee fo r the current year, when that Emp loyee has less than twelve
( 12) months of service to the Sheriff' s Office.
The Employee shall pay this amount not as penalty, but as agreed upon liquidated damages, in the
event that said Employee terminates sa id employment with the Sheriff during training within the
first twelve ( 12) months subsequent to taking the oath of office.

4.

In no event s hall liq uidated damages, as set fo rth above, be assessed if the Employee fai ls to
satis facto rily complete the training. o r termi nates his or her employment during the first twelve
(12) months, due to disabling ill ness or inj ury, verified by a physician of the Sheriff's choice.

5.

The exceptions as set forth in paragraph four ( 4) above shall not apply in the event that there is a
substantial evidence that the Employee has been dismissed as a result of mis representing his or
her basic qualifications for employment, or has caused his or her dismissal, fail ure. illness or
injury in an attem pt to avoid payment of liquidated damages set fort h above.

2296

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY I 0, 200 I
6.

Damages assessed herein wi ll be prorated according to the amount of training completed, in the
event said damages should become payable prior to the Employee taking the oath of office after
the completion of the training period required by the Sheriff's Office.

7.

Said Employee acknowledged that he or she meets the basic qualifications for employment as set
fort h by the Sheriff.

8.

Said Employee also states that the information placed on his or her formal application and that
given to personnel conducting any background investigation is accurate and complete to the best
of his or her knowledge.

9.

In the event that the Employee is called to active military duty, or has his or her probationary
period extended for any reason whatsoever, or is granted a leave of absence during any period of
time contemplated by this Agreement, the period of said Agreement shall be extended
accordi ngly.

I 0.

This Agreement shall become effective upon Empl oyee's official starting date and shall remain in
full force and effect for twelve ( 12) months following admi nistration of the oath of office, unless
extended as provided in paragraph nine (9) above.

I I.

This Agreement is to be construed in accordance with the laws of the State of Illinois, and
embodies the entire agreement between the parties hereto, and each party acknowledges that there
are no inducements, promises, terms, conditions or obligations made or entered into other than
those contai ned here in.

I 2.

Thi s Resolution shall take effect for all Employees hi red by the Sheri ff's Office after the approval
of thi s Resolution by the Cook County Board of Commissioners.

Commissioner Moran, seconded by Commissioner S ilvestri, moved to defer consideration of the
Proposed Reso lution to the August 9, 200 I Board meeting. The motion carried unanimously.

* * * * *
Subm itting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
EARLEAN COLLINS, County Commissioner
Co-Sponsored by
ROB ERTO MALDONADO, County Com missioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

A RESOLUTION CALLING UPON U.S. PRESIDENT GEORGE W. BUSH
TO INSTITUTE A MORATORIUM ON THE BOMBING OFF THE ISLAND
OF VIEQUES AND TO PERFORM AN ENVIRONMENTAL ASSESSMENT
OF THE EFFECTS OF THE NAVY'S BOMBING TO THE ISLAND
AND THE SURROUNDING WATERS OFF ITS COAST
WHEREAS, the Island of Vieques is part of the mainland of Puerto Rico which is a commonwealth of
the United States and is known as the Commonwealth of Puerto Rico; and

2297

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 10, 200 1

WHEREAS, the Commonwealth of Puerto Rico receives financial assistance and protection from the
United States; and the people of Puerto Rico are United States citizens and should share in all of the rights
and privileges of any other citizen; and
WHEREAS, in 1942, the Navy acquired 26,000 of the 33 ,000 sq uare acres of the Island of Vieques,
leaving only 7,000 acres for the residents of the Island of Vieques; and
WHEREAS, military exercises have destroyed the agricultural lands and contaminated the costal waters
and marine life with bombardments and ruined the livelihood of the island's fi shing community ; and
WHEREAS, in 1983, a Memorandum of Understanding (MOU) was signed by the Secretary of the U.S.
Navy, James Goodrich and the Governor of Puerto Rico, Carlos Romero Barcelo wherein it was agreed
that safety would be increased ; endangered species would be protected; jobs and economic development
wou ld be established; and the bombing would end; and
WHEREAS, the bombing has not terminated and many innocent lives have been lost due to the errors in
the bombing exercises which continue to contaminate the waters and destroy agricultural land; and
WHEREAS, since April 1999, the people of Puerto Rico and their representatives have demanded a
permanent end to the bombing and thereafter have demonstrated and protested the Navy's misuse of the
island.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commiss ioners of Cook County hereby
cal ls upon the President of the United States and Congress to institute a moratorium on military bombing
exercises on the Island of Vieques and conduct an independent study to assess the environmental impact
on the citizens and marine life on the Island; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of thi s Resolution be tendered to the President and
Members of Congress and spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorab le Body.
Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commi ssioner Collins, seconded by Commissioner Sil vestri , moved that the Proposed Resolution be
refen-ed to the Committee on Legis lation and Intergovernmental Relations. (Comm. No. 244842). The
motion carried unanimously.

PROPOSED CONTRACT RENEW AL
Transmitting a Communication from
TERRY A. STECZO, Deputy Assessor for Administration & Taxpayer Services
requesting authorization for the Purchasi ng Agent to renew Contract No. 99-43-1256 with Risetime, Inc.,
Schaumburg, Illinois, to proceed with Phase 2 of the Assessor' s Office Automation Project, to be
implemented by Risetime, Inc. T hi s phase includes Computer Assisted Mass Appraisal (CAMA)
software, legacy system interfaces, business process re-design and integration services.
Reason:

The Automation Project contract provides a definition of Phase 2, once the design of Phase I
has been completed. Phase I has been substantially completed by the project team now
employed by Risetime, Inc. Their knowledge of the Assessor's Office procedures, their
computer system expertise, and their knowledge of and fami liarity with the systems des igned
in Phase I will enable them to implement Phase 2 most efficiently and effectively.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $6, 125,000.00. Contract period: July I 5, 2001 through November 30, 2002.
(7 I 5/040-579 Account). Requisition No. I 0400475.

the C lerk's Office. The NCSC, in conjunction with a steering committee, wi ll de fine the appropriate
changes in business process and the technology needs of the Clerk's Office and provide recommendations
fo r business change and alternative technology solutions.
Reason:

T he National Center for State Cout1s is a private, no n-profit agency with more than 29 years
of experience in assisting courts in determining and devising solutions to court iss ues. In
add ition, the NCSC has developed a cadre of specialists in the various aspects of court
operations and will draw upon many of these individuals in this project.

Account)). One time purchase. Requisition Nos. 13350003 and 13420209.

2317

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 10, 200 1
PROPOSED ORDINANCES
Transmitting a Communication from
DA YID ORR, County Clerk
PROPOSED ORDINANCE
VITAL R ECORDS FEES FOR THE COUNTY CLERK
WHEREAS, the Cook County Clerk maintains marriage, birth, and death records for Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the 92nd Illinois General Assembly passed H.B. 3054, a bill that amends the Yitai Records
Act; and
WHEREAS, H.B. 3054 requires county clerks and local registrars to charge a $2.00 fee for each certified
copy of a death registration, in addition to any other fees charged by county clerks and loca l registrars;
and
WHEREAS, H.B. 3054 provides that the $2.00 fee must be transmitted to the State Registrar monthly
and deposited into the Death Certificate Surcharge Fund for the purpose of imple menting a statewide
electronic reporting system for death registrations and for other purposes; and
WHEREAS, it is expected that the Governor will sign H .B. 3054 into law, which would take immedi ate
effect; and
WH EREAS, the City of Chicago currently charges $10.00 for first copies of death certificates and $2.00
fo r additional copies; and
WHER EAS, the Cook County Clerk currently charges $7.00 for fi rst copies of death certificates and
$2.00 for additional copies.
NOW TH E R EFORE BE IT ORDAINED AS FOLLOWS:
Section l. The Cook County Clerk shall continue to charge and collect a fee of $7 .00 for the first copy,
and $2.00 for each additiona l copy of a birth record.
Section 2. The Cook County Clerk shal l continue to charge and collect a fee of $7 .00 for the first copy,
and $2.00 for each add iti onal copy of a marriage record.
Section 3. The Cook County Clerk shall charge and collect a fee of $10.00 for the first copy, and $4.00
for each additional copy of a death record.
Section 4. The fee increase for death records shall become effecti ve upon passage of this Ordinance, but
not until such time as H.B. 3054 becomes law.

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Sims, moved that the Proposed Ordinance be
referred to the Committee on Finance. (Comm. No. 244839). The motion carried unanimously.

23 18

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY I 0, 200 I

* * * * *
Transmitting a Communication, dated July 9, 200 I from
DA YID ORR, County C lerk
PROPOSED ORDINANCE

LEGAL DESCRIPTION AUTOMATION FEE FOR THE COUNTY CLERK
WHEREAS, the Cook County Clerk maintains records of official legal descriptions on over 2 million
current and fom1e r permanent real index numbers in Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the only fonnat in which these records currently exist is a manual copy of the records
created since the institution of the permanent real estate index system over forty-fi ve years ago; and
WHEREAS, the County Clerk would like to both preserve and automate these legal descripti on records
so legal descriptions can be accessible in conjunction with the countywide G IS; and
WHEREAS, the County Clerk's Office is currently working to imple ment the GIS project through
review and analys is of digitized versions of the Clerk's official county tax maps and ancillary property
records; and
WHEREAS, the Ind ustrial Engi neeri ng Section of the Bureau of Administration has determined that the
cost to prod uce a legal description upon request justifies an increase in the fee to help defray costs to
automate and preserve these records; and
WHEREAS, the Industrial Engineers have further determined that is very important that all complete
legal descriptions be accessible through the county's new GIS system and that there is no other source
available for this information:
NOW THEREFORE BE IT ORDAINED AS FOLLOWS:
That the County C lerk shall charge and collect a fee of $3.00 from each party who
Section 1.
purchases a copy of a legal description in the County of Cook to be deposited in the (County) C lerk's
Automation Fund;

Section 2.
This fee shall be in addition to all other fees and charges of the Clerk and shall be
remitted monthly by the Clerk to the County Treasurer in the special fund designated as the C lerk's
Automation Fund;
Section 3.
after passage;

The County C lerk shall commence such charges and collections beginning two weeks

Section 4.

This Ordinance shall become effective upon passage.

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved that the Proposed Ordinance be
referred to the Committee on Finance. (Comm. No. 24484 1). T he motion carried unanimously.

RESOLUTION
Transmitting a Communication, dated June 19, 2001 from
WA LL Y S. KOS, P.E., Superintendent of Highways
Completion of Construction Approval Resolution
Quentin Road, Baldwin Road to Dundee Road
in the Village of Palatine
Section: 82-V6246-03-RP
Final Cost: $4,24 1,630.28
The contract price of this project was $4,283,201.80, and final cost is $4,241 ,630.28. The decrease was
due to B.C. No. 1 through 2, approved by the County Board as the job progressed, and B.C. No. 3, the
final adjustment of quantities.
01-R-501
RESOLUTION

APPROVAL RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the highway improvement known as Quentin Road from Baldwin Road to Dundee Road
with Section: 82-V6246-03-RP with work on Quentin Road, removal of the existing two lane bituminous
pavement and the construction of two 24 foot wide standard reinforced P.C. Concrete Pavements flanked
by Combination Concrete Curb and Gutter, overlaying Subbase Granular Material, separated by a 16 foot
mountable median with channelization at intersecting streets, and from Station 300+60 to Station 308+60
widening the existing pavement wi th Subbase Granular Material, Bituminous Base Course and
Bituminous Concrete Binder Course and resurfacing with Bituminous Concrete Surface Course,
transitioning from 4 lanes to 2 lanes and including a 3 foot paved shoulder; on Dundee Road, removal of
the existing 3 lane bituminous pavement and the construction of a variable width (32.6 foot to 54 foot)
P.C. Concrete Pavement flanked by combination concrete curb and Gutter or P.C. Concrete Shoulders,
overlaying aggregate subgrade and on both Quintin Road and Dundee Road, removal and reconstruction
of all street returns and driveways, removal of unsuitable material in the subgrade and replacement with
porous granular embankment, special and suitable embankment material, construction of temporary bypass pavement with temporary steel sheet piling req uired at the deepest area of unsuitable material
excavation, guardrail construction, construction of an enclosed storm sewer system with its associated
drainage structures, traffic signal reconstruction at the intersection of Quentin Road and Dundee Road,
parkway restoration with topsoil and sod or seed, signing, pavement marking, and other related roadwork,
has been regularly awarded by the Board of County Commissioners for construction as a County
Highway improve ment, and

2331

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY JO, 2001
WHEREAS, the aforesaid highway improvement has been satisfactorily completed in accordance with
the provi sions and stipulations of aforesaid contract, now, therefore
BE IT RESOLVED, that the work and construction of aforesaid contract be, and hereby, is approved.
July 10,200 1

Commissioner Carr, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved that the Approved Resolution be
approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

the fourth year of a four-year program to provide detention alternatives for juvenile transfers.

detention for juveniles who are transferred to adult court for trial and are thus inel igible for juvenile

of the Ch ief Coordinator, Bureau of Public Safety and Judicial Coordinatio n, for a one ( 1) year period for
the GIRLS LINK program. This extensio n is necessary because of RF P revisions, extended contract
negotiations and an amended time li ne of accomplishments.
G IR LS UNK of Cook County is a gender-responsive initiative sponsored jointly by the U.S . Department
of Justice, Office of Juvenile Justice and Delinquency Prevention (OJJDP), and by the Bureau of Justice
Assistance. Its obj ecti ve is to pos itively impact g irls deemed at ri sk or already involved in the juveni le
justice system. The Illinois Juvenile Justi ce Commi ssio n through the Division of Communi ty Health
Prevention of the Illinois Department of Human Services awarded GIRLS LINK this grant to critically
review the efforts of the GIRLS LI N K co llaboration to date. The grant will fund a study to ascertain what
works to reduce rec idi vism among delinquent girls, to increase family in volvement in the li ves of these
girls, and to heighte n community awareness of the unique issues raised by girls in the juvenile justice
system. The results of this study w ill benefit Cook County and w ill enhance gender-responsive progress
nation wide.

An Ordinance A mending the Cook County Building C ode Re: Construction Fencing
(Ordinance Amendment)
W HEREAS, the County of Cook is a Home Rule unit in accordance with the Constitution of the
State of Illi nois of 1970; and
WHEREAS, the County has the authority to adopt ordinances and promulgate rul es and
regulations that pertain to its government and affairs that protect the health, safety and welfare of its
citizens.
NOW, THEREFOR E, BE IT ORDAINED by the Pres ident and the Board of Commiss io ners of
Cook County, Illino is that the Cook County Building Code incorporate the following ordinance:
Article IV General Provisions
Section 4.4-3

2373

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY I 0, 200 I

Construction Fencing
A.

If a permit authorizes demolition or authori zes construction of a new principal structure or
s ubstantial excavation , then the applicant shall cause a safety fence to be installed around the
s ubject property in a location and manner approved by the department.
The protective fencing herein required shall be at least six feet high in height and be of
substantial construction capable of preventing persons from falling into such excavation or
construction or otherwi se being injured by virtue of such work.

The fencing s hall be installed not more than seven (7) days nor less than four (4) days before
the commencement of any work on the s ubject property, including mass grading and the installation
of site utilities, pursuant to any permit issued by Cook County. Said fe ncing shall remain in place
until a certificate of occupancy is issued for the structure. The location of the perimeter fencing may
be changed during the construction period with approval of the Building and Zoning Department.
"No Trespassing" signs shal I be mounted on the fencing in conspicuous locations around the site. If
the size of the construction site is too large for fencing a lone to be effective, in the judgment of the
Building and Zoning Department, the permittee must have the construction area patrolled by a
licensed Illinois detective agency during the hours specified herein for the closing and locking of
gates.
B.

Any gate in a perimeter fence must be closed at all times except to allow ingress and egress to
and from the site. Said gate must be locked at all times, other than permitted hours of
construction specified in Section 4.5 of the Building Code and at any other time when no
work is being performed on the site.

C.

Fencing, as provided herein, shall also be required for any construction project of Cook
County, school or park district, or any other public agency, whether or not a building permit
has been or is required to be iss ued by Cook County when the project is located within any
area in which Cook County has authority and jurisdiction.

D.

Fencing, as provided herein, shall a lso be required around any activity, whether a bui lding
permit is required or not, where construction or landscaping materials are stored or
stockpiled.

No Certificate of Occupancy shall be issued for any construction undertaken in conjunction
with the provisions of this ordinance until such time that al l penalties and fines have been resolved to
the satisfaction of the County.
Section 3

This ordinance shall be in full force and effect from and after this day of passage.

Approved and adopted this 10th day of July 2001.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

239540

COOK COUNTY BUILDING CODE ORDINANCE (PROPOSED ORDINANCE
AMENDMENT). S ubmitting a Proposed Ordinance Amendment sponsored by Gregg Gosli n
and Peter N. Silvestri , Co-sponsored by John P. Daley, Carl R. Hansen, Roberto Maldonado,
William R. Moran and Mike Quigley, County Commissioners:
PROPOSED ORDINANCE
An Ordinance Amending the Definition of Building Height
(Proposed Ordinance Amendment)
Whereas, the definition of building height in the Cook County Bui lding Ordinance is
ambiguous and contradictory on the issue of measuring height in the absence of curbs; and
Whereas, due to this oversight significant grade changes have become an ongoing problem in
unincorporated Cook County going forth relatively unfettered by County Ordinance; and
Whereas, a small change in the definition of building height will add ress thi s contradictory
language by clarifying the manner in which building height is meas ured when there is no curb
present;
NOW THEREFORE BE IT ORDAINED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that
the Cook County Building Code be amended as follows:
Building Code
Artic le II
Page JOA
Building Height: is the vertical distance measured from the curb level or its equivalent
opposite the center of the front of the building, to the highest point of the under side of the
ceiling beams in the case of a flat roof; to the deck line of a mansard roof; and the mean level
of the under side of the rafters between the eaves and the ridge of a gable, hip, shed, gambrel,
or any othe r pitched roof. Where no curb level has been established the height of a building
shall be measured from the mean elevation of the finished existing lot grade at the front of the
building.

Commissioner Goslin, seconded by C ommissioner Ha nsen moved to accept the Substitute
Ordinance. T he motion carried.
Commissioner Goslin, seconded by Commissioner Daley, moved the approval of the Substitute
Ordinance. T he motion carried.

An Ordinance Amending the Definition of Building Height
(Ordinance Amendment)
Whereas, the definition of building height in the Cook County Building Ordinance is ambiguous and
contradictory on the issue of measuring height in the absence of curbs; and
Whereas, due to this oversight significant grade changes have become an ongoing problem in
unincorporated Cook County going forth re latively unfettered by County Ordinance; and
Whereas, a s mall change in the definition of building height will address this contradictory language
by clarifying the manner in which building height is measured when there is no curb present;
NOW THEREFORE BE IT ORDAINED, by the Cook County Board of Commiss ioners that the
Cook County Building Code be amended as follows:
Article Ill Rul es and Definitions

Building Height is the vertical distance measured from the curb level or its equivalent opposite the center
of the front of the building, to the highest point of the under s ide of the cei li ng beams in the case ofa flat
roof; to the deck line of a mansard roof; and the mean level of the unde r side of the rafters between the
eaves and the ridge of a gable, hip, shed, gambrel, or any other pitched roof. Where no curb level has
been established the height of a building shall be measured from the mean elevation of the fini shed
existing lot grade at the front of the building.

REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE ON FINANCE
June 26, 2001
The Honorable,
The Board of Commissioners of Cook County

ATTENDANCE
Present:

Chairman Daley, Commissioners Butler, Goslin, Hansen, Maldonado, Moran,
Moreno, Quigley, Silvestri , Steele and Sutker ( 11 )

Absent:

Vice Chairman Carr, Comm issioners Collins, Lechowicz, Schumann and Sims (5)

Excused Absence:

President Stroger ( 1)

Also Present:

John Chambers - County Comptroller; Grace Colbert - Director of Budget and
Management Services; Sharon Gist-G illiam - Vice President of Unison Maximus and
forme r City of Chicago Budget Director; and Sandra K. Williams - Secretary to the
Board of Commi ssioners

Court Reporter:

Barbara Small, C.S.R.

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Finance of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant to notice on
Tuesday, June 26, 2001 at the hour of 10:00 A.M. in the Board Room, Room 569, County Building, 118
North C lark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Sandra K. Williams, Secretary to the Board of Commissioners, announced a revised Transfer of Funds
packet was delivered to the Commissioners earlier.

2378

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 10, 2001
Commissioner Hansen noted that the figures in the Appropriation Trial Balance are difficult to read
because of the fo nt size. He said he hoped to receive a revised document that would be easier to read and
asked that the totals be placed in the front of the document instead of the back. He indicated there is no
percentage on the amount of time of the year e lapsed in the fiscal year, to measure against the percentage
of expenditures out of the adjusted appropriations.
John Chambers, County Comptroller, stated that the font will be increased and the percentages of the year
expired will be added.
C hairman Daley asked Grace Colbert, Director of Budget and Management Services, to explain the
purpose of the Transfer of Funds meeting.
Ms. Colbert explained that a budget is an estimated spending plan and in order to realign any
appropriation, the Board authori zation is necessary during a transfer of funds meeting. She added, once
into the fiscal year, if it is determined that certain line items are under- or over-estimated, then the line
items are realigned. She said the debt is shuffled and the departments cannot exceed the original
appropriation. Ms. Colbert concluded by stating that since 1995, transfers requested have always been
less than two percent.
Commissioner Quigley asked if the majority of departments use surplus funds from vacant positions? He
asked ifthe Budget Department was aware of certain trends in the transfer requests since 1995?
Ms. Colbert responded that the 110 Account (Salaries and Wages of Regu lar Employees) is the largest
area from which transfers are made and are usually taken from vacant positions.
Comm issioner Quigley stated that based on the information provided, it could be assumed that transfers
of funds is a permanent system that creates contingencies so departments can transfer fund s at will midyear. The Commissioner further stated that this blindsides the budgetary process and said in time he
hopes transfer requests will be less than half of one percent.
Chairman Daley stated that prior to budget approval, all commissioners have the opportunity to reduce the
budget by offering amendments that could eliminate positions in departments.
Commissioner Si lvestri asked about procedures used by other units of government with regard to
transfers of funds.
Chairman Daley stated that in some cases, other governments may allow fund transfers without approval
by a legislative body. For example, the C ity of Chicago operates under different rules. Leave was
granted for Sharon G ist-Gilliam to explain this further.
Sharon Gist-Gilliam, Vice President of Unison Maximus and former City of Chicago Budget Director,
stated that the Cities and Vi llages Act of the Illinois Revised Statutes controls what and how
municipalities can transfer funds. She said the City of Chicago is a special section of the Act and it
all ows transfers among the objects of appropriation within the categories of appropriation. City
departments must present their requests to the City Council by a certain date before a transfer can be
approved. She added that moving monies from one line item to another within contractual services, as an
example, does not require approval; however, if a department requests to transfer funds from contractual
services to materials and supplies, then the department must seek approval from the City Counci l.
In response to Commissioner Quigley's statements, Commissioner Steele said the transfer process is
designed to allow some flexibility in the budgetary process.

2379

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY I 0, 200 I
Commissioner Hansen said he believes the current transfer process provides the Budget Depattment with
accurate information on how to budget for the next year based o n any line item adjustments in the current
year's budget. He said if the Board allows the departments to make adjustments without approval, the
Board runs the risk of not being aware of these budgetary changes. The Commissioner noted that
emergency transfer req uests can be brought before the Finance Committee at any time. Commissioner
Hansen acknowledged that historically the total yearly transfers are less than two percent, which is a
minimal amount for a budget that is $2.7 bi llion and 27,000 employees.
Chairman Daley has submitted questions to departments as part of the record. (The referenced documents
are on file in the Office of the County C lerk.)
The Committee considered requests from various departments to transfer appropriations between
budgetary accounts. Chairman Daley proceeded to the requests for transfers of funds under $I 0,000.
They are as follows:

Commissioner Quigley requested detai led information regarding vacant positions and what transfers have
been requested on an annual basis from departments. The Commissioner said that he wants the Board to
be able to see if certain patterns exist in the transfer requests from a desire to have flexibil ity or simply to
adjust line-items in mid-year.
Ms. Colbert clarified that the information that Commissioner Quigley has requested is currentl y available,
but changes each pay period. She acknowledged that the budget is based on every department
maintaining a 3% vacancy factor at all times. She noted that 100% of the vacant positions are not fu nded
and staffing is at a 97% level. Ms. Colbert concluded by stating that it is up to each department to
manage the vacant positions in a way in which 3% of the funding is not spent.

Commissioner Butler moved to adjourn. Seconded by Commissioner Moreno, the motion carried
unanimously and the meeting was adjourned.
Transcripts for this meeting are available in the Office of the Secretary to the Board, I 18 North Clark
Street, Room 567, Chicago, lllinois 60602.
Respectfully submitted,
COMM ITTEE ON FINANCE
JOHN P. DALEY, Chairman

fixation right iliac crest bone graft to relieve chronic back pain). State's Attorney, Richard A.

REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE ON CONSTRUCTION
June 21 , 2001
The Honorable,
The Board of Commissioners of Cook County

ATTENDANCE
Present:

Chairman Carr, Vice Chairman Butler, Commissioners Collins, Hansen and Silvestri (5)

Absent:

Commissioners Moreno and Sims (2)

Also Present:

Calvin R. Sutker, Commissioner (1); Michael LaMont - Director, Office of Capital
Planning and Policy; David A. Roth - Senior Consultant, Lerch, Bates & Associates; and
Patricia Shymanski - Interim Chief of Staff

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Construction of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant to notice
on Thursday, June 21, 2001 at the hour of 2:00 P.M. in the Board Room, Room 569, County Building,
118 North C lark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Committee has considered the following item(s) and upon adoption of this report, the
recommendations are as follows:
244389

OFFICE OF CA PIT AL PLANNING AND POLICY, by Michael E. LaMont, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated June 12, 2001:
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for authorization for the Purchasing
Agent to advertise for bids for the County Wide Elevator Modernization Phase II, Bid
Packages 5, 6 and 7. It is respectfully requested that this Honorable Body approve this
request.

2471

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY I 0, 200 I
This project provides for modernization of elevators that will be divided into three different
bid packages. Package 5 will provide for work on 11 elevators at the Rockwell Warehouse
and the Department of Corrections parking structure; Package 6 will provide for work on 19
elevators at Oak Forest Hospital of Cook County and the Durand and Hektoen buildings at
Cook County Hospital ; and Package 7 will provide for work on 13 elevators at the 4th and
6th District Courthouses.
Bond Iss ue (20000 Account).
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.

*Referred to the Construction Committee on 6/1 9/01.
Chairman Carr asked Michael LaMont to explain the reason for the fiscal impact increase.
Michael LaMont responded that the increase is due to the addition of the two escalators located in the
Cook County Building on the Randolph Street side that go down to the Vital Statistics Department. He
said originally the escalators were going to be modernized after the City of Chicago built the pedway to
the County Building, but the C ity of Chicago informed the County that the City is no longer building the
pedway. He stated that the project adds about $0.5 million to the budget request.
Commissioner Hansen asked the location of the two escalators?
Michael LaMont reiterated that the escalators are located in the Cook County Building on the Randolph
Street side.
Commissioner Silvestri asked what would the escalator modernization provide?
David Roth, Lerch, Bates and Associates, stated that the escalator modernization consists of a total
replacement of all the parts inside the escalator, including steps, axles, bushings, and chains that would
bring the escalators up-to-code. Mr. Roth said the life of an escalator is between twenty-five and thirty
years. He also stated that the escalators have reached the end of their useful life. Finally, Mr. Roth stated
that it is becoming more difficult for current maintenance providers to obtain parts for the escalators and
it is time to replace them.
Chairman Carr asked Mr. LaMont to explain the county-wide elevator modernization.
Michael LaMont referred to the back-up materi al, " Summary of the County-W ide Elevator
Modernization" that highlighted the condition of the 354 elevators throughout Cook County. Mr. LaMont
stated that in 1999, he requested approval of a $24 million county-wide program for elevator and
escalator improvements. The Office of Capital Planning and Policy evaluated all county escalators and
elevators and the units were categorized as poor, fair, good and excellent. Currently, there are four
moderni zation contracts and when those contracts are complete the number of units that are now poor and
fair will drop and the amount of escalators and elevators in excellent condition will increase.
Mr. LaMont further stated that if the request before the committee today is approved and once the project
is completed, within two years the County will be at a point between good and excellent for almost 90%
of all the elevators in the County. He concluded by stating that most of the poor units are in the old Cook
County Hospital and the old Children's Hospital and are not being upgraded because they are slated for
demolition.

2472

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 10, 2001
Commissioner Collins asked how the elevators in the County Building are rated?
Michael LaMont stated that the elevators are in either good or excellent condition. He said a complete
rehabilitation was done in the early 1990s and there have been occasional problems but all have been
renovated.
Commissioner Collins asked the total amount allocated for the project.
Michael LaMont responded the amount allocated is about $24 million.
Commissioner Collins asked how much has been spent so far?
Michael LaMont stated that he does not have an exact amount at this time, but will have it for the
Commissioner after the meeting.
Commissioner Hansen asked what steps are being taken now to ensure that the elevators do not reach the
42% level in the future?
Michael LaMont stated that a continuing program is not needed because of the full modernization but in
five to ten years a mid-term modernization may be necessary in addition to standard elevator
maintenance.
Commissioner Hansen asked if there is any kind of a program that keeps up with the expenditure and
maintenance of the elevators before they fall into the poor condition?
Michael LaMont asked David Roth from Lerch, Bates and Associates to respond to Commissioner
Hansen's question.
David Roth stated that the County is currently performing spot audits and during these spot audits, Lerch,
Bates and Associates randoml y selects elevators and escalator units to audit. Technicians physically go to
the job site to perform audits on units that are measured against industry performance standards. All
deficiencies are reported to the maintenance contractor who has a thirty day-time frame to correct any
deficiencies. He concluded that Lerch, Bates and Associates photographs and documents all deficiencies
in reports.

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Vice Chairman Butler,
Communication No. 244389, as amended. The motion carried.

REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE ON HEALTH AND HOSPITALS
June 26, 200 I
The Honorable,
The Board of Comm issioners of Cook County

ATTENDANCE
Present:

Chairman Butler, Commissioners Daley, Goslin, Hansen, Maldonado, Moran,
Moreno, Quigley, Silvestri, Sims, Steele and Sutker ( 12)

Absent:

Vice Chairman Schumann, Commissioners Carr, Collins and Lechowicz (4)

Exc used Absence: President John H. Stroger ( I)
Also Present:

Ruth Rothstein - Chief, Bureau of Health; Dr. Lynda Brodsky - Director of Research
Affairs; and Dr. Peter Orris - Professor of Preventive and Internal Medicine, Rush
University College of Medicine

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Health and Hospitals of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met purs uant
to notice on Tuesday, June 26, 200 I at the hour of 11 :00 A.M. in the Board Room, Room 569, County
Building, 118 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Committee has considered the following items:
I.
2.
3.

Informati on on how the Institutional Review Board (IRB) functions throughout the Bureau of
Health Services
Review the functions, process and concerns of the Institutional Review Board ( IRB)
Reviewing and understanding the federal guidelines that regulate all research in volving human
participants

2479

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY I 0, 200 I
Following the Roll Call, Chairman Butler made remarks regarding the purpose of the meeting. He stated
that in 1986 when he was elected a county commissioner, there were research issues at Cook County
Hospital regarding the use of dilantin, and most commissioners did not realize this drug was being used in
research cases at the hospital. As a result, Chairman Butler decided it would be prudent to discuss these
bio-ethical issues before the Health and Hospital s Committee to inform the commissioners of the
guidelines used in research activities.
Ruth Rothstein stated that at one time each institution had their own review board but now the Bureau of
Health Services has consolidated these boards into a single Institutional Review Board (IRB). Further,
Ms. Rothstein stated that Dr. Peter Orris, Chairman of the Institutional Review Board, would give a slide
presentation and discuss the function of the board and federal guidelines that regulate all research
involving human participants. Chief Rothstein introduced Lynda Brodsky, Director, Research Affairs, as
well as the other members of the Institutional Review Board: Dr. Bradley Langer, Dr. Madhu Malhotra,
Dr. Linda Murray and Dr. Aaron Hamb.
Dr. Orris stated that the Institutional Review Board was established to protect the rights and welfare of
human subjects in research activities; and said a review of any project is based on three ethical
foundations: I) respect for persons; 2) beneficence; and 3) justice.
Dr. Orris said the IRB recognizes the personal dignity and anonymity of each individual and the
individual is given an informed consent as to whether they want to participate in the research activities.
He said if they choose not to participate, they must understand that their medical care will not be
impacted. He further stated research is voluntary and for those who participate, do so out of a desire to
improve medical knowledge.
Dr. Orris continued that all research has some risk because the research involves comparing a known drug
to one that may be better based on both animal and human experiments. He said patients must understand
this ri sk and it is the obligation of the Institutional Review Board to make certain there is a balance
between the safety of the patients and any risk. Finally, Dr. Orris said that the benefits and burdens of the
research are to be fair and that the ri ghts of patients are to be protected within the process.
In response to Commissioner Hansen ' s question, Dr. Orris defined research as the desire to improve
medical knowledge.
Commissioner Sutker questioned when a hospital advertises for research, whether the ad indicates the
possibility of side effects from the drugs. He also asked about liability issues and if patients sign waivers.
Dr. Orris stated that he does not believe there have been any liability issues involving any studies the
Institutional Review Board has undertaken. He further stated an attorney from Risk Management and an
Assistant State's Attorney are present at all meetings.
Commissioner Moreno asked how many studies are currently underway at the Bureau, in what research
areas and what other research the hospital would like to undertake?
Dr. Orris said he would respond in writing to the question.
Chairman Butler asked Ms. Rothstein to give a closing statement.
Ruth Rothstein stated she believed today' s meeting was successful and educational. She said each month
a grants newsletter is distributed to County Board members from Lynda Brodsky' s office that may answer
questions commissioners have or they can contact the Bureau of Health Services.

2480

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY I 0, 200 I
Commissioner Hansen stated that the meeting and the presentation were very helpful and suggested that
other meetings be held in the future.

Commissioner Daley moved to adjourn the meeting, seconded by Commissioner Goslin.
motion carried and the meeting was adjourned.

Respectfully s ubmitted,

JERRY BUTLER, Chairman

242356

TOWN OF CICERO (NO CASH BID REQUEST.) Transmitting a Communication, dated
March 19, 200 I from Deborah Sims, Chairman, Tax Delinquency Subcommittee, submitting
a request from Judd M. Harris, Attorney.

2481

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY JO, 2001
The Town of Cicero is requesting tax certificates from the No Cash Bid Program for the tax
delinquent properties in the submitted list.
The intended use of the parcels is for public purposes including but not limited to : parking
lots, green space and play lots. Submitted is a copy of Resolution number 78-01 , in which
the Town of Cicero formally requests the no cash bid for these parcels. Also included are
Sidwell maps of each parcel. A photograph and current title search of each parcel will be
given to the Board within the week. In add ition, Fredda Berman, attorney for the Cook
County Clerk, has been notified of the proposed no cash bid on these parcels and has sent out
the necessary thirty-day letters required under lllinois law.
The Town of Cicero has retained Judd M. Harris, Esq. to file petitions for tax deeds for the above
mentioned parcels.
Fredda Berman, Director of Real Estate Services, stated that parcels 16-21-035-007, 16-21-309-012, 1622-102-010, and 16-28-219-00 1 are available for a No Cash Bid purchase, but are subject to prior tax
sales that could yield tax deeds to buyers from the 1999 Scavenger Sale. She said if a deed is awarded,
the court will require payment of the delinquent taxes, and if this occurs after a No Cash Bid sale, then
payment of the delinquencies would be in the fonn of redemption.
Commissioner Carr asked if one of the parcels is a business that owns adjacent prope1ty, but is not paying
taxes on it?
In response to Commissioner Carr's question, Troy Deckert, Department of Planning and Development,
answered that his department is not sure that the business owns the property. The business is a restaurant
that has a parking lot next to it and there are tax delinquent lots located next to those parcels that are being
used as additional parking for the restaurant.
Commissioner Moreno asked how many lots are being considered on the No Cash Bid for C icero?
Chairman Sims answered 22 lots are being considered.
Commissioner Moreno asked if the County has the exact addresses of these properties?
Ms. Berman responded the exact addresses are not known, however the County can establish commonly
known addresses for these properties.
Commissioner Moreno indicated, in late March 2001, the subcommittee approved the transfer of
approximately 42 lots to Cicero on a No Cash Bid basis. He said the request was to use the parcels for
public purposes, play lots, parking lots and other public interest purposes. The Commissioner asked if
there is a manner in which the County can track exactly what will ultimately happen with these lots.
Ms. Berman responded that the Department of Planning and Development requires participants in the No
Cash Bid process to come back to inform the department of the status of the purchases.
Mr. Deckert added that the Department of Planning and Development requests annual reports that the
Department compiles and transmits to the Board of Commissioners. The report includes every parcel
approved as a No Cash Bid.
Chaim1an Sims stated a copy of the annual report would be available to all the comm issioners.

2482

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 10, 2001
Commissioner Moreno asked if the parcels are transferred by way of sale to an existing business if the
County tracks the purchasers and the purchase price amount?
In response to Commissioner Moreno's inquiry, Mr. Deckert indicated that all public records are included
as well as the names of the developers. The law does not require the purchase price to be listed but the
question is asked and if a business is identified in advance, an affidavit is signed attesting that they did
not previously own the property and are not a part of any de! inquent taxes.
Commissioner Moreno asked if the City of Chicago has sole discretion as to who receives these
properties as well as for what purposes?
Mr. Deckert answered that all municipalities negotiate with developers. He said it is a decision made by
the municipalities and voted on by that legislative body.
Commissioner Moreno inquired if requests must be sent directly to the municipality or is it possible to
have the requests conveyed to a 50 l-C3, non-profit organization?
Mr. Deckert acknowledged that the usual procedure is to have the property conveyed to a municipality
because back taxes are cleared and the municipality conveys the parcel(s) to a private developer or nonprofit organization. He said a municipal exemption allows complete wipe-out of the taxes.
Commissioner Collins asked ifthere is a time limit as to how long a property can be held before selling it
or conveying it to another entity?
Mr. Deckert answered that there are annual reports sent to the Department of Planning and Development
from the various municipalities that can be made available to the Board.
Randy Kemmerer, State's Attorney ' s Office, answered that the properties can be held for an extended
amount of time.
Commissioner Goslin asked how long properties remain on annual reports?
Mr. Deckert answered the properties are listed on the reports as long as they are vacant, land banked and
are reported for five years or until the development is completed.
Mr. Deckert requested Judd Harris, Assistant State's Attorney for the Village of Cicero, to address the
subcommittee.
Mr. Harris stated that PIN 16-21-306-032 was deeded to the Town of Cicero in June 1998 and then a tax
deed was issued to American National Bank and Trust Company. He said that the land trust is not one
over which the Town of Cicero has control. It is a subsequent deed and having no known challenges
recorded within two years following the date of deed, and the assumption is a valid title would have been
conveyed. It is hard to say what would have happened if the Town of Cicero had contested the tax deed.
The Town of Cicero was probably made a necessary party in the litigation that led to American National
Bank being named as trustee in October 1998. He noted that counsel for the Town of Cicero, Beth Janaki
Clark, had previously addressed the specifics and substantive issues of the deed with Mr. Deckert.
Mr. Deckert asked if there is anything relevant about PIN 16-21-400-025?
Mr. Harris responded there was a lawsuit about five years ago and does not know the basis of the lawsuit.

2483

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY I 0, 200 I
Mr. Deckert stated that if the lawsuit is not relevant that the Department of Planning and Development
would not object to the parcel being approved and recommends its consideration.
Mr. Deckert referenced PIN 16-22-102-0 I 0 that shows the Department of Transportation. He said his
concern is whether this is some government ownership of the land.
Mr. Harris said there does not appear to be any government interest that would preclude the parcel from
being considered as a No Cash Bid.
Mr. Deckert referenced PIN 16-22-100-006, and said a title search was not received by the Department of
Planning and Development and therefore recommends deferral of this PIN .
Commissioner Moreno referenced PIN I 6-21-306-013 and asked if the parcel was conveyed to American
National Bank and Trust under a trust that would eventually be utili zed to acquire three Cicero owned lots
and two other parcels to construct a Walgreen's Drug Store on Cermak? He inquired if a broker was used
and ifthere are restrictions on monies attained by the municipalities on the sale of such lots?
Mr. Harris could not provide an answer to Commissioner Moreno' s question.
Mr. Deckert said in general, monies attained from sales go to the general fund but in reference to
Commissioner Moreno' s question, he would respond later to the subcommittee.
Commissioner Collins asked ifthe property has to be sold at market value or does the municipality make
the total decis ion on how much and to whom they want to convey it?
Chairman Sims responded that the municipality makes all the decisions.
Chairman Sims stated there are nine parcels not available for approval.
Ms. Berman indicated that the reason parcels 16-20-205-026-0000, 16-20-307-018-0000, 16-21-100-0l 10000, 16-21-205-022-0000, 16-21-205-023-0000, 16-21-209-027-0000, 16-21-306-012-0000, 16-21-308009-0000 and I 6-22-100-005-0000 are not available is because there are not two years of delinquent

SOUTH SUBURBAN TAX REACTIVATION PROJECT (NO CASH BID REQUEST).
Transmi tting a Communication dated June 5, 200 1 from Deborah Sims, Chairman, Tax
Delinquency Subcommittee, submitting a req uest from James M. Houlihan, Cook County
Assessor.

2485

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 10, 200 1
Please accept this letter as the South Suburban Tax Reactivation Project's formal No Cash
Bid request on behalf of Dixmoor, Harvey, Markham, Phoenix, Richton Park and Robbins.
The listing includes the permanent index number and volume of each real estate parcel.
These parcels will be used for commercial and industrial purposes. The South Suburban Tax
Reactivation Project will retain legal counsel to obtain the tax deed and will bear all legal and
other costs associated with acquisition of the parcels.

South Suburban Tax Reactivation Project
2nd Round No Cash Bid Requests
June 5, 2001
The following is a synopsis of the list ofrequested parcels:

Dixmoor
15 parcels

Harvey 3rd Party
6 parcels

Markham
5 parcels

Phoenix
21 parcels

Richton Park
I parcel

Robbins/KPMG Site
5 parcels

Metra Station
20 parcel s
Mr. Deckert stated the Department of Planning and Development has identified 9 parcel s that are owned
by the Village of Phoenix and should be withdrawn. One parcel could be approved, but it has a Cook
County lien that may require payment by the Village in the future.
Mr. Deckert referenced the Village of Markham and asked if there is occupancy?
Gregory Carney, Project Director, South Suburban Tax Reactivation Project, responded that according to
the Markham attorney and city inspectors, the sight is vacant and there is no business establishment.
Mr. Deckert referenced the Village of Dixmoor and inquired if people are living in the town home
parcels. He indicated he wants to insure that the people are given proper opportunity to relocate before
the town homes are sold.
Mr. Carney said he met with the officials of Dixmoor who informed him that the area has been designated
for a commercial strip by the City Council. Mr. Carney said that property owners will be given fair
market value.

2486

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 10, 200 I
Chairman Sims said that the subcommittee wants to make sure that no one is displaced.
Chairman Sims asked ifthe people are renters?
Mr. Carney answered renters as well as squatters reside on the property.
Mr. Deckert asked what is the planned use for PIN 29-07-141-043 in the Village of Dixmoor on Sibley
and Hoyne?
Mr. Carney answered the intent is for commercial redevelopment. He stated the church does not own the
property but it is as an extended parking lot. The Village has permitted church parking to date but seeks
commercial use. The church will be notified.
Mr. Deckert said he recommends consideration of John's Arrow Transmission in Harvey and expects the
third party affidavit from the business owner.
Mr. Carney then provided the documents to the Department of Planning.
Mr. Deckert indicated the following PINs 29- 16- 131-077, 29-16-131-08 1, 29-16-131-082, 29-16-13 1083, 29-16-131 -084, 29-16-131-085, 29-16-131-086, 29-16-131-087 and 29-16-207-049 are owned by
the Village of Phoenix should not be approved.
Chairman Sims indicated that the Village of Robbins has been withdrawn.
Mr. Carney referenced the Village of Robbins and stated that the Village of Robbins was going to pursue
additional PINS that would provide for an expansion of the current Metra station. He said Metra is tax
exempt and may create a number of opportunities, such as commercial economic development. He added
Jackie Harder, Director, Department of Economic Development feels that this is appropropriate. Mr.
Carney concluded by saying that the Village of Robbins plans to make this request at a later time.

Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Commissioner Collins, moved the approval of Communication
No. 244398, as amended. The motion carried.

VILLAGE OF SOUTH CHICAGO HEIGHTS (NO CASH BID REQUEST). Transmitting a

Heights:
Re:

Village of South Chicago Heights
No Cash Bid Application 2001-1
Acquisition of Sauk Steel - PIN: 32-33-102-022-0000

The purpose of this letter is to inform you of the Village of South Chicago Heights' desire to
participate in the Cook County No Cash Bid Program. The Village is interested in acquiring
the above referenced commercial property located in its community. The real estate taxes
have been delinquent for two or more years; therefore, pursuant 35 ILCS 200/21 -90 it is
eligible for a No Cash Bid.
Please accept this request to obtain the above referenced property. The Village plans to
acquire this property on behalf of third-party applicant Turfts Grinding, Inc. Tufts Grinding,
Inc. has been an established business in South Chicago Heights for several. Tufts plant is
adjacent to the old Sauk Steel building and intends to incorporate the Sauk Steel sight into its
physical plant.

2487

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY JO, 200 1
As part of this request, the Village has submitted all the information that is required by the
Cook County Board of Commissioners to enable South Chicago Heights to participate in this
program. Tufts Grind ing, Inc. and the Village of South C hicago Heights have retained the
services of an attorney to proceed to a tax deed and perform all other legal activities
associated with this program.
Ms. Berman indicated that there had been a previous scavenger sale and the tax purchaser is going ahead
with this process and so it wi ll be very likely the property will not be avai lable to the Village of South
Chicago Heights because the tax sale will need to be redeemed by the prior scavenger sale buyer.
Ken Pi Iota, Attorney, Village of Chicago Heights, stated that the tax buyer in question has a hi story of
be ing in this situation and never takes the properties to deed.

ORDINANCE
Transm itting a Communication, dated June 14, 200 1 from
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President, Cook County Board of Commissioners
I transmit herewith a proposed Ordinance to be considered by this Honorable Body.
This Ordinance has been recommended by the Department of Labor of the State of Ill inois, pursuant to
the Wages of Employees on Public Works ( Prevailing Wage Act, Illinois Revised Statutes, codified as
amended, 820 ILCS 13011 et seq. ( 1993), formerly Ill. Rev. Stat., Ch. 48, par. 39s- 1 et seq.).

01-0-18
ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, the State of Illino is has enacted "An ACT regulating wages of laborers, mechanics
and other workers employed in any public works by the State, county, city or any public body or any
political subdivi sion or by any one under contract for public works," approved June 26, 194 I, codified as
amended, 820 ILCS 130/ J et seq. ( 1993), formerly Ill. Rev. Stat., Ch. 48, par. 39s- I et seq.; and
WHEREAS, the aforesaid Act req uires that the Board of Commi ssioners of the County of Cook
investigate and ascertain the prevailing rate of wages as defi ned in said Act for laborers, mechanics and
other workers in the locality of said County employed in performing construction of publi c works, for
said County.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED BY THE PRESIDENT AND BOARD OF
COMMISSIONERS OF THE COUNTY OF COOK:
Section 1.
To the extent and as req uired by "An Act regulating wages of laborers,
mechanics and other workers employed in any public works by the State, county, city or any public body
or any political subdivision or by any one under contract for public works," approved June 26, 1941 , as
amended, the general prevailing rate of wages in this locality for laborers, mechanics and other workers
engaged in the construction of public works com ing under the jurisdiction of this County is hereby
ascertained to be the same as the prevailing rate of wages fo r construction work in the Cook County area
as determined by the Department of Labor of the State of Illinois as of June 200 l , a copy of that
determinati on being attached hereto and incorporated herein by reference. As required by said Act, any
and all revisions of the prevailing rate of wages by the Department of Labor of the State of Illinois shall
supersede the Department's June determination and apply to any and all public works construction
undertaken by the County of Cook. The Definition of any terms appearing in this Ordi nance which are
also used in aforesaid Act shall be the same as in said Act.
Section 2.
Nothi ng herein contained sha ll be construed to apply said general prevailing rate
of wages as herein ascertained to any work or employment except public works construction of this
County to the extent required by the aforesaid Act.

2489

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JULY 10, 200 1

Section 3.
The Bureau of Human Resources shall publicly post or keep available for
inspection by any interested party in the main office of this Bureau of Human Resources (County) this
determination or any revisions of such prevailing rate of wage. A copy of this determination or of the
current revised determination of prevailing rate of wages then in effect shall be attached to all contract
specifications.
Section 4.
The Clerk shall mail a copy of this determination to any employer, and to any
association of employers and to any person or association of employees who have fi led their names and
addresses, req uesting copies of any determination stating the particular rates and the particular class of
workers whose wages will be affected by such rates.
Section 5.
The Bureau of Human Resources shall promptly file a certified copy of this
Ordinance with both the Secretary of State Index Division and the Department of Labor of the State of
Illinois.
Section 6.
The Bureau of Human Resources shall cause to be published in a newspaper of
general circulation within the area a copy of this Ordinance, and such publication s hall constitute notice
that the determination is effective and that this is the determination of this public body.
Section 7.
The Purchasing Agent of Cook County shall specify in the call for bids in any
contract for public works that the general prevailing rate of wages in the locality for each craft or type of
laborer or mechanic needed to execute the contract to perform s uch work, also the general prevailing rate
for legal holiday and overtime work as ascertained by the Bureau of Human Resources, shall be paid for
each craft or type of work needed to execute the contract or to perform such work. The Purchasing Agent
in awarding the contract shall cause to be inserted in the contract a stipulation to the effect that not less
than the prevailing rate of wages, as found by the Bureau of Human Resources, shall be paid to all
laborers, workers and mechanics performing work under the contract, and the Purchasing Agent s hall al so
require in a ll such contractor's bonds that the contract include such provision as will guarantee the faithful
performance of such prevailing wage c lause as provided by the contract.
Section 8.
In the case of any underpayment of the prevailing wage, a penalty of 20% of the
underpayment shall be assessed against the contractor or subcontractor; and the 20% penalty shall be
payable to the Illinois Department of Labor. Any underpayment that has not been repaid to a worker
within thirty-days of violation is s ubj ect to an additional 2% of the underpayment as a punitive damage
assessment. This is payable to the worker.
Section 9.
There is an automatic two (2) year debarment of any contractor or subcontractor
found to have violated the Act on two (2) separate occasions. An affected contractor or subcontractor
may request the Department to hold a hearing on the al leged violations within ten ( IO) days notification
of the second violation.
IL. DEPT. OF LABOR PREVAILING WAGES FOR COOK COUNTY EFFECTIVE 06/01/01
DIVISION OF CONCILIATION & MEDIATION

WHEREAS, Almighty God, in His infinite wisdom, has called 8th Ward Alderman Lorraine L. Dixon,
from our midst; and
WHEREA S, appointed to the City Council in 1990, Alderman Dixon was a tireless advocate, not only for
the people of her ward, but for all of Chicago; her personality was dynamic and she was a firm believer in
working together to accomplish great things; and
WHEREAS, throughout her distinguished career, Alderman Dixon accomplished a number of impressive
" firsts," such as being both the first African-American and the first female alderman to serve as president
pro tempore of the Chicago City Council; and
WHEREAS, as the first female to chair the City's Budget and Government Operations Committee,
Alderman Dixon never allowed herself to get distracted by the power and prestige of the position; she
remained true to her primary objective: to serve the public; and
WHEREAS, a genuinely dedicated and committed public servant, Alderman Dixon always looked for
unique and creative ways to increase opportunity and improve the quality of life for her constituents; she
co-sponsored the city's first contractor and vendor fair which provided a wealth of information and
demystified the process of how minority- and women-owned businesses could gain the necessary
certification to do business with the City of Chicago; and
WHEREAS, as a person who truly personified the word " service" in public servi ce, Alderman Dixon,
even during her final days with us, continued to make rounds throughout her ward, taking notes to assess
what was going on and what work needed to be done; and
WHEREAS, definitely her own person, Alderman Dixon always stood strong and had no problem
confronting tough and emotional issues head-on such as slavery reparations and other matters of concern
to her community; and
WHEREAS, the myriad contributions Alderman Lorraine Dixon made to the 8th Ward, the Democratic
Party, the City of Chicago and the governmental arena were significant, far-reaching and will forever
resonate.

contain a curriculum with cultural, traditiona l and historical components designed to enhance the selfesteem of migrant Mexican students and promote a deeper understanding of their roots. The prog ram
fosters an understanding of 2000 years of Mexican hi story and includes an explanati on of cultural and
trad itio nal celebrati ons to students of various grade levels; and

WHEREAS, Rosie Lee Jackson-Lattin was a long time member of the Pilgrim Rest Baptist Church of
Be ll City, Missouri until wedd ing Mr. C.Q. Lattin . She then jo ined St. Matthews Baptist Church of Cape

Honoring Leo Stec on bis 50th Birthday
WHEREAS, Leo Stec was born on July 25, 195 1 in Lowell, Massachusetts and will reach the
milestone of his 50th birthday on July 25, 2001; and
WHEREAS, Leo Stec graduated from Providence College in Rhode Island; and
WHEREAS, Leo Stec has been married to his wife Nancy for 25 years and is the father of Sarah
and Katie; and
WHEREAS, throughout hi s 50 years Leo Stec has unselfishly given his time and energy to his
community and many worthy causes; and
WHEREAS, Leo Stec is the Chief Operating Officer and Managing Partner of Saturn of
Glenview and Saturn of Chicago; and
WHEREAS, Leo Stec was e lected to the Glenview C hamber Board of Directors in 1995 and
served as Chairman of the Local Government Affairs Counsel from 1996- 1999 and is cun-ently the
C hairman of the Board and serves on the Chamber Executive Committee; and
WH EREAS, Leo Stec is an active member in his community, contributing his time and talent to
a variety of causes and projects including Glenview Park Di strict Foundation and St. Catherine LaBourre
Church; and
WH EREAS, Leo Stec is also a member of the Optimist Club of G lenview and the Sunrise Rotary
Club of Glenview; and
WHEREAS, Leo Stec received the 2000 Business Person of the Year Award,
Glenview Chamber's highest honor; and

considered the

WHEREAS, we recognize the auspicious occasion of Leo Stec's 50th Birthday and his many
accomplishments thus far.
